Public Security Organs Must Not Handle Opium Cases Arbitrarily

Notice from the County Government

The Shanghai County Government issued a notice yesterday, stating that the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs had instructed the Opium Prohibition Committee to investigate. Since the promulgation of the new opium prohibition law, the penalties for opium offenders have become more severe. As a result, opium offenders often prefer to bribe the public security organs to settle the case rather than being transferred to the court after being arrested. Although investigators have found no conclusive evidence, the opium offenders are afraid of further offenses and remain silent, and the public security personnel are even more reluctant to disclose the illegality. This situation will not only hinder the opium prohibition efforts but also give the public security organs an opportunity to accumulate wealth. Therefore, it is proposed that in the future, if people intentionally offer bribes to escape the law, once the investigation confirms the facts, the bribe-givers and bribe-takers will be punished according to the law, and the bribes will be recovered and confiscated. If anyone misunderstands the provisions of the opium prohibition law, mistakenly believes that the penalty is for a minor offense, and does not intentionally offer a bribe, they may not be punished according to the law if they truthfully state the facts to the authorities and provide supporting evidence. If people come forward to report bribery and the investigation confirms the facts, the bribe-givers and bribe-takers will be punished according to the law, and the bribes will be recovered and a portion of the recovered bribes will be awarded to the informants in accordance with the regulations for rewarding opium prohibition fines, so as to prevent abuses and emphasize opium prohibition. The committee discussed and resolved to adopt the above proposal, and the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Judicial Administration have successively replied with their approval and suggestions. In addition to notifying the relevant parties separately, we hereby request you to investigate and instruct your subordinates to comply with and publicize the matter. It is hereby ordered that the director of the department instruct the county bureaus to comply with and implement the order strictly and issue a public notice. If public security personnel handle opium cases arbitrarily again, they will be subject to dismissal and punishment according to the law, without any leniency. This is the order. In addition to distributing this notice, we hereby order the county magistrate to instruct the director of the Public Security Bureau to comply and issue a public notice to inform the public and conduct inspections at all times without any leniency. This is the order. In addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau to comply, we hereby issue a public notice to inform the people of the county. This is the notice.

Silk Factories Urge Suspension of Public Weight Inspection

The decline of the silk market in this port has reached its extreme. In addition, the spun silk is piled up in foreign warehouses and is difficult to sell. Since April 1st, the Silk Inspection Bureau has adopted public weight measurement for export factory silk, and the manufacturers have suffered losses. They appealed to the trade association to find a way to provide relief. Therefore, the Shanghai Silk Factory Association convened a temporary general meeting of all manufacturers at 4 pm the day before yesterday (18th). More than 90 people attended, chaired by Shen Huachen. At the meeting, the representatives respectively expressed the losses suffered by the export factory silk since the implementation of the public weight inspection. According to past facts, it is estimated that the annual cost of each factory is more than 10,000 yuan or at least 1,000 yuan. The silk industry is in a critical situation, how can it withstand this heavy burden? Moreover, the public weight inspection is only implemented in Japan among the silk-producing countries. Its situation is completely different from that of Chinese silk. The reason why Japan implements public weight measurement is that silk is spun with new-style silk reeling machines and spun by sinking reeling method, and then undergoes re-reeling (commonly known as Yang Fan). Cocoons are cooked thoroughly with cocoon cooking machines and drawn with warm water. Not only do they not use water heaters to dry, but also take water again after re-reeling, so the moisture content is relatively heavy. At that time, the export merchants stationed in Japan suffered a lot of losses because Japanese silk contained too much moisture, so they proposed public weight trading to show fairness, and the government of Japan knew that if Japanese silk was not corrected for moisture, it might not be able to stand in the American market in the silk-selling country, so it agreed to the public weight system to maintain the original position of international trade with the United States and then expand it. This is the fact that Japan implements public weight in the sale and purchase of raw silk to the United States. The reeling method of our country's raw silk exports has always been boiled water floating reeling, that is, the Italian-style mechanical reeling method. Not only is boiling water used for reeling, but also there is a close water heater to promote drying when the silk is sent to the silk box. The silk is moved to the silk room and has a larger water heater to make it completely dry, so except for the climate, it is not as moist as Japanese silk. The two are completely different, and it is obvious that Chinese silk is not suitable for public weight. Moreover, in the past 60 years of China's raw silk trade with foreign countries, European and American buyers have never had any disputes with Chinese silk due to moisture content. Now the trial implementation of this public weight has been nearly six months. The advantages and disadvantages are obvious. If the public weight system is not abolished by the end of this month, the factories will have to close down and wait to avoid being sacrificed in vain. The public is extremely angry, so the committee of the trade association agreed to print the records and send a letter to the Inspection Bureau to explain the unsuitability of the trial implementation of public weight in order to comply with public opinion and stop it as scheduled before October 1 to avoid accidents. The meeting adjourned at 7 pm.

Minutes of the Executive Committee Meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Third Meeting

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its third standing meeting of the executive committee at 4 p.m. yesterday. Committee members Wang Xiaolai, Ye Huijun, Wang Yansong, Gu Xinyi, Yuan Ludeng, Lao Jingxiu, Chen Songyuan, Lu Qisheng, Cheng Xiechun, Xu Qilu, Wu Zhihao, Li Jiaobo, Lu Wenshao and other twenty people attended. Chairman Wang Xiaolai performed the formalities. After the secretary reported on the chamber's affairs, the following cases were discussed: (1) Discussing the consolidation of various public bonds of the former chamber of commerce. It was found that the public bonds issued by the former chambers of commerce were directly raised by the chamber of commerce itself and should be treated differently from other debts. The consolidation should be carried out as soon as possible and the method of repayment and the independent management of the fund should be determined to maintain the chamber's credibility. The total debt of the General Chamber of Commerce's construction bonds is more than 138,000 taels of silver, and more than 15,800 taels of silver is mortgaged. The total debt of the County Chamber of Commerce's construction bonds is more than 60,500 taels of silver. The total debt of the three is more than 230,000 taels of silver. If a method is not determined quickly, the interest on the debt will increase and the burden will become heavier. A comprehensive plan should be made to determine a concrete main case based on 30% of the annual membership fees and the income from rent so that it can be fundamentally consolidated and implemented. (Resolution) To organize an examination committee, Xu Jiluo, Gu Xinyi, Pei Yunqing and others were elected as the committee together with the original proposer to conduct a detailed examination. (2) Discussing the urging of stores that have not yet formed trade associations to prepare for establishment. It was found that Article 2 of the revised implementation rules of the Trade Association Law stipulates that if there are more than seven companies in the same region, they must organize an association in accordance with this law so that they can unify business operations. The association should officially announce and set a deadline for them to prepare for establishment and conduct investigations to list and prepare for reference as a basis for urging. (Resolution) Passed. (3) Discussing the standardization of the names of important employees of companies and stores. It was found that the affairs of commercial companies and stores currently represented by shop owners are very complicated in this city. Their names include general manager, assistant manager, manager, deputy manager, chief manager, and deputy manager. The varieties are different. They generally choose one of the titles they have always used arbitrarily and do not have a certain standard. Outsiders who have dealings with the company may suddenly hear this name, and it is almost impossible to distinguish whether they can represent the company for all rights and limits. It was found that the titles of general manager and assistant manager of commercial companies were stipulated in the company regulations of the previous Qing Dynasty, and there is no basis for them today, so it is difficult to apply them again. The titles of chief manager and deputy manager are only used by companies organized by Cantonese merchants. There is no other basis for them, and the names are not popular. Moreover, the commercial laws and regulations promulgated recently, such as the company registration regulations and the implementation rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law, all refer to the person in charge of the affairs of the company or store as the manager. It seems that the name of manager has a legal basis and is more common and popular in commercial habits. In order to determine the responsibilities and make it easier for the general public to understand, it is said that this name must be standardized. It is proposed that all important employees of commercial companies and stores who are currently called general manager, chief manager, or other similar names should be uniformly changed to manager. Those who are called assistant manager, deputy manager, deputy chief manager, or other similar names should be uniformly changed to deputy manager. Those who are managers serving in the head office or head store should be changed to general manager to distinguish them. If the resolution is passed, it is proposed to submit it to the Bureau of Social Affairs for approval and announcement. (Resolution) Submit to the Bureau of Social Affairs. (4) Discussing the draft rules for the Chamber of Commerce to accept events. (Resolution) Revised and passed. These rules will be implemented temporarily for one year. (5) Discussing the Chamber of Commerce's announcement of the current situation. (Resolution) Passed and sent immediately.

The Constitution Revision Committee of the Chinese Red Cross Society held its thirteenth meeting at 2 pm on September 18. The committee members present were Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Ye Zhisheng, Dong Xinqin, Wang Peiyuan, Wu Jiasan, Xu Xichun, Jiang Daqiu, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Hong Yanbin, Yang Ke, Xue Shaoting, etc. Chairman Wen Lanting, Recorder Wei Ruifeng, performed the formalities and read the minutes of the previous meeting. (1) Dong Xinqin said that Article 15 should be changed to: Members' motions should be discussed in order in accordance with the meeting procedure. Petition for Relief from Various Counties in Western Liaoning

The Jisheng Society and He Fenglin, Zhang Jixin Communicate Via Telegram: The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received telegrams from members of the Liaoning Society, He Fenglin and Zhang Jixin, addressed to Wang Yiting and others of the Chinese Jisheng Society. The telegrams stated: "The counties along the west of our province are located in the lower reaches of various rivers. Since July 3rd, heavy rains have fallen continuously, causing mountain floods. In just a few days, more than ten counties in the western region have become a watery expanse. The most severely affected are Suizhong, Jin County, Panshan, and Xinmin. Jixin, on official business, passed through Yuguan and witnessed the devastation firsthand. It is estimated that the area covered by the floods along the Beining Railway is six to seven hundred li long and two to three hundred li wide, a vast expanse of water. Over ten thousand people have drowned, hundreds of thousands of acres of farmland have been submerged, and countless houses have been washed away. Although officials and gentry of this province have cooperated in planning urgent relief efforts and have set up porridge kitchens in various counties, the disaster area is too large and the disaster situation is too severe. At present, there are no fewer than several hundred thousand disaster victims awaiting relief, without clothing or food, a truly unbearable sight. Urgent relief is currently underway, but autumn, winter, and spring relief will follow in succession. Where the water has receded, sand and silt have been deposited to a height of one or two zhang, making cultivation impossible for two to three years. Relief efforts cannot be delayed even for a moment. Over the years, our society's righteous porridge and benevolent grains have reached nearly the entire country. We will certainly be deeply concerned about the disaster situation in the Northeast this time. We are making a life-saving appeal on behalf of our elders and brothers, seeking assistance. We also know that our society has been providing relief to the provinces of Henan and Shaanxi for years, and our resources are becoming depleted. However, Shanghai has abundant goodwill and numerous charitable organizations. A single call will elicit a response from all quarters. We respectfully request that you, elders, unite various charitable organizations to cooperate in appealing for donations to continuously provide relief and save these dying disaster victims. The people of Liaoning Province will be eternally grateful. Our society's benevolent influence is widespread, and we are especially grateful for your extraordinary assistance. Because of our official duties, we are unable to come in person. We respectfully recommend Mr. Shan Zhongfan as our representative to discuss and handle matters nearby. In addition to separate telegrams from various senior officials of our province, we hereby submit this telegram to report the situation." Regarding the urgent relief and winter relief for the Liaoning Province flood, the society has entrusted Mr. She Guisheng, the director of relief efforts in Tianjin, to handle the matter at his discretion. In response to the telegram mentioned above, a reply was immediately sent stating: "To Mr. Zhang Shuzhun, Chief of the General Affairs Department of the Northeastern Political Affairs Committee in Fengtian, and forwarded to Mr. He Maoru, and addressed to Chairman Wang and Mr. Xiao: We have received your telegram and are fully aware of the situation. We previously received a telegram from Mr. She Guisheng, the director of relief efforts in Tianjin, reporting the severity of the disaster in Liaoning Province. Our society has entrusted Mr. She Guisheng to handle the matter at his discretion. As you mentioned in your telegram, our society has been stretched thin due to the widespread disasters in the provinces of Shaanxi, Henan, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang. We have exhausted all our resources, and telegrams and letters requesting relief are pouring in like snowflakes, leaving us at a loss as to how to cope. However, given the severity of the disaster in your region, our colleagues will do everything possible to provide winter relief, which will still be handled by Mr. She Guisheng. As for your request for Chairman Wang, Huang, and Xu to contact charitable organizations and appeal for donations, we will discuss the matter and do our best to assist. We hereby reply to your telegram. We hope you will take this into consideration." Disasters are widespread, and the disaster areas are expanding daily. Relief efforts are difficult to provide comprehensively. Where can we find thousands of spacious mansions and hundreds of zhang of fur coats to help these orphans and prevent them from filling ditches?

Revival Movement of Domestic Films

Domestic films were once a sensation several years ago. Since the opening of American talkies in various cinemas in this city, they were initially very prosperous. However, audiences dwindled daily because talkies mostly focused on singing and dancing, and the plots were often far-fetched. Moreover, language barriers greatly reduced audience interest. Luo Mingyou, a famous movie star in North China, was aware of this and recently united domestic celebrities and colleagues to organize the China Film Industry Company. It is reported that the Great China, Lily, and Minxin Film Companies in this city have all joined. It is also reported that Mrs. Zhang Yu Fengzhi from the Northeast and Sir He Dong from the South are both directors of the company. If the company determines its purpose and strives to arrange and produce diligently in the future, the revival of domestic films can be realized, and it will not be a problem to compete with foreign films.

Temporary Light Installation on Yuxingnao Lighthouse

Public Notice from the Inspectorate Division of the Maritime Customs Department: This division has investigated that the Yuxingnao (also known as Xifu Island in the nautical charts) lighthouse under the jurisdiction of the Jianghai Customs Tax Office is undergoing a change of its original lighting equipment to install temporary lights. The details are listed below. The Yuxingnao Lighthouse in Dinghai County, Zhejiang Province, will undergo a change of equipment between October and November of this year. During the change period, two temporary lights will be installed on the observation platform of the lighthouse, one on the north side of the platform and one on the south side of the platform. They will be lit around October 15th, and no further notice will be given. They will use sixth-order acetylene quick-flashing lights, flashing once every three seconds, with a flash duration of three-tenths of a second. In clear weather, they will be visible for about 18 nautical miles. Once the original light is changed, it will be re-lit, and no further notice will be given. However, the characteristics of the light will change from intermittent to flashing, flashing white twice every twenty seconds. The light intensity will be increased to 55,000 candlepower. All temporary lights will be removed simultaneously when the original light is re-lit. This notice is hereby issued for compliance. All vessels should pay close attention and remember these details to avoid negligence. Be mindful and do not forget. This notice is issued on September 15th of the 19th year of the Republic of China.

Western Paint Industry: Liu Zongyuan, a member of the Western Paint Industry Trade Association, has been leasing houses in Ji Jia Lane, owned by Wu Taihe Tang, for many years. The rental payments have been made monthly, and the rights and obligations have been fulfilled according to the contract, with no disputes. Now, according to a letter from the representative lawyer, Wang Huangong, the contract must be revised. Member Liu believes this is unreasonable and requested the association to reply based on the facts. The association replied yesterday as follows: "To whom it may concern: Member Liu Zongyuan of our association has stated that he received a letter from lawyer Wang Huangong, which stated: 'We are instructed by our client, Wu Taihe Tang, to inform you that all lease contracts for the houses leased by our firm must be revised to conform to a unified standard. We have been specially commissioned to protect and represent the interests of our client. Please come to our law firm to discuss all matters.' Our member has leased houses from Wu Taihe Tang for many years, and the rights and obligations have been fulfilled according to the contract, with no differences. The rent has been paid monthly without any arrears, and there has been no infringement of property rights. What is there to protect? We request that your firm reply based on the facts.' Based on the above, we hereby reply as follows. We hope that your lawyer will review this and inform your client." Addressed to lawyer Wang Huangong.

Local News 2

Liu Tongyun, Manager of Fu Ji Paper Store, Kidnapped

Just Entered Car to Return Home

Bandits Jumped Aboard

Driver Expelled and Injured

Extortion Letter Received Beforehand

At 8:10 last night, a kidnapping occurred suddenly at the Chun Geng Lane entrance of Da Gou Bridge across from the Big Ben patrol station on Eduya Road, Public Concession. The kidnapped victim was Liu Tongyun, manager of Fu Ji Foreign Paper Store at No. 45 Chun Geng Lane. At the time, the bandits fired six or seven shots as a warning, fortunately without injuring anyone. The car driver was expelled midway and sustained a serious head injury. The details are as follows:

Borrowing a Car as Transport: Liu Tongyun, 54 years old, from Ningbo, is currently the manager of Fu Ji Foreign Paper Store at No. 45 Chun Geng Lane, Shandong Road entrance of Eduya Road. The store was established more than ten years ago, and although the business is thriving, it is merely a broker for the Fuji Paper Manufacturing Company, a Japanese company. The commissions earned are also very small. However, Liu's natural diligence has won the trust of the Japanese. Recently, the Fuji Company temporarily lent him a car to use as transportation because of his exceptional hard work. The car is a sedan, license number 6233 (City 2216).

Sudden Gunshots: Liu's residence is located at No. 434 Pu Bai Road in the French Concession. Yesterday afternoon, Liu went out from his home, first to the Fuji Company at No. 14 Guangdong Road, and then to Chun Geng Lane. At 8:10 in the evening, Liu was accompanied by three or five friends from Fu Ji, intending to return to his residence by car. Just as he entered the car and nodded goodbye to his friends, the car driver, Yang Afu (44 years old, from Tongzhou), was about to start the engine when suddenly a gunshot was heard near the back door of the Big Ben patrol station across the road.

Driver Unable to Resist: At the sound of the gunshot, five bandits suddenly rushed out from the roadside, each holding a handgun, and jumped into the car. One bandit pointed a gun at the car driver's mouth, forbidding him to make a sound. Three bandits held Liu in the center, forcing him to drive. The car driver initially attempted to resist, but fearing a repeat of the Fan Dongshan incident on the Jin Shenfu Road the other day, he started the engine and drove west. At this time, another five or six gunshots were fired suddenly, all into the sky, so no one was injured. It is assumed that bandits were lying in ambush on all four sides nearby, fearing that the neighboring patrol stations would be alerted, in order to temporarily resist arrest.

Friends Stood Like Wooden Chickens: At that time, the friends who were seeing Liu off all stood at the entrance of the alley, standing like wooden chickens, watching the car drive west. The two guards at the Chun Geng Lane entrance also cowered and retreated into the alley to avoid stray bullets. When the car reached the Shi Yu Lane entrance of Zhengjia Wood Bridge, one bandit expelled the car driver, Yang Afu, who sustained a serious head injury. The car continued to drive west. Afu was seen by the patrol officer at that location, who, after inquiring about the details, immediately took him to the Big Ben patrol station to report. The patrol chief immediately ordered detectives to drive and pursue the bandit car, but it had already disappeared without a trace. The car driver was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment by the detectives.

Received Extortion Letter: After the incident, the Central Patrol Station heard the news and immediately sent Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. According to a staff member of the store, they had received an extortion letter from the bandits two months ago, demanding a large sum of money. The wording in the letter was extremely aggressive, but Mr. Liu did not report it to the patrol station, and over time, he forgot about it. It was truly unexpected that he would be kidnapped now. The patrol station is conducting a thorough investigation, but the car has not been found as of this morning.

Seventeen-Year-Old Girl Narrowly Escapes Execution in Bandit Den

Wang Xiangyi Redeems Her for Thirty Yuan

Girl Overjoyed and Willing to Offer Herself

Neighbor Finds Her But She Is Unwilling to Go Home

Wang's Appearance is Strange and Evil, Seemingly Non-Human

Beautiful Girl: Wu Wenlong, a 17-year-old girl from Tongzhou, is beautiful in appearance. Her family has lived near Jinsha Town outside the East Gate of her hometown. Her parents are both alive, and the family's financial situation is considered to be fairly well-off. In recent years, bandits have infested the area north of the Yangtze River, committing murder, arson, kidnapping, and extortion. Any resident with slight savings is targeted by these individuals, either for robbery or kidnapping. Wu Wenlong's family had long been coveted by the bandits. After learning that Wenlong was betrothed to someone but had not yet married, her father cherished her like the apple of his eye. First, they sent a threatening letter to Wu Wenlong's father, Ronglian, but he ignored it. The bandits then resorted to a final measure: on the dark night of April 11th of the old calendar year, they went to Wu's house and knocked on the door. Ronglian, unaware, opened the door to greet them. The bandits rushed in and abducted Wenlong from her bed. Before leaving, they ordered her father to prepare money for ransom.

Prepared for Execution: After Wenlong was abducted, her father thought that the kidnapping of people by bandits in the countryside was commonplace. If he prepared a ransom immediately, the bandits would consider her a valuable asset and demand a huge sum. It would be better to ignore them temporarily so that the bandits would think they had no ability to redeem her and might release her. Therefore, Ronglian ignored the bandits' repeated letters urging him to pay the ransom. Wenlong, with her delicate beauty, fell into the bandit's lair and was inevitably ravaged by the bandits. After a month, the bandits, seeing that the girl's father had not yet come to negotiate, took Wenlong out on May 12th, intending to tear up the ticket and shoot her.

Redeemed for Her Life: Wang Xiangyi, 26 years old, also from Tongzhou, at that time led Wenlong out from under the bandits' guns, hid her in his home, and told her that he could not bear to see an innocent girl die by gunshot, so he spent 30 yuan to redeem her. He asked her where she wanted to go in the future. Wenlong, hearing this, considered him a great benefactor, was extremely grateful and tearful, and voluntarily offered herself to him. The two lived together for several days, then moved to Shanghai, living near Pingliang Road in Yangshupu. Wang made a living by pulling a rickshaw, but the cost of living in Shanghai was high, and his income was barely enough to make ends meet. They managed to survive for two months before running out of money. They then decided to return to their hometown.

Came to Shanghai to Search: Wenlong's father, Ronglian, learned that his beloved daughter had escaped from the bandit's lair and had been taken to Shanghai by someone. He entrusted his neighbor, Ji Xiaomapi, to come to Shanghai to search for her. After arriving in Shanghai, Ji rented a place to live on Xizang Road in the Public Concession and also made a living by pulling a rickshaw. During his free time, he searched for Wenlong's whereabouts, but the city was vast and the population was dense, and he never found any trace of her. He had no choice but to return to his hometown and report back. Wang also took Wenlong and left Shanghai to return to their hometown. He secretly sold some of the family property, and his finances were slightly improved. So, he arranged everything and came to Shanghai again to make a living.

Met on a Boat: The other day, the man and woman took the Baohua steamer from their hometown port to Shanghai. Initially, they did not know that Ji Xiaomapi was still entrusted by the girl's father to search for Wenlong in Shanghai for the second time. As fate would have it, he actually came to Shanghai on the same boat with Wenlong and Wang. They recognized each other on the boat, and Ji urged Wenlong to quickly return home to avoid her family's expectations. Unexpectedly, Wenlong had been with Wang for a long time and changed her mind. She immediately expressed her willingness to live with Wang and that the matter of returning home would have to wait for another day. Ji, hearing this, did not argue with her. Yesterday morning at 2:00 a.m., the boat arrived in Shanghai. Wang and Wenlong hired a sampan to cross the river, and Ji also hired a boat to follow them. Ji immediately reported to the patrol police at the Muddy Beach Ferry, and Wang and the girl were taken to the Third District.

Sent to Court for Trial: Zhang District Chief interrogated the three people. Ji claimed that he was entrusted by his neighbor, Wu Ronglian, to come to Shanghai twice to search for his daughter. Now that his goal has been achieved, he requests permission to take Wenlong back to her hometown. Wenlong stated that after being abducted from her home by the bandits, she initially lived in the countryside, moving east and west, and there was no fixed address. Sometimes they moved several times a day to avoid the eyes and ears of the authorities. The bandits all had ferocious faces and looked extremely terrifying. When these individuals held secret meetings, they hid me in a secret room, and my freedom was completely restricted. I was at their mercy, and if I resisted even slightly, I feared for my life. On May 12th, the bandits suddenly wanted to shoot me. I saw no hope of survival, but unexpectedly, a savior suddenly appeared. Wang Xiangyi spent 30 yuan to redeem me and save me from death. Wang is my savior, so I am willing to be at his disposal. Although my family is extremely expectant, there will eventually be a day of reunion, but I will not go back for the time being.

Seemingly Not a Good Person: Wang Xiangyi's account of how he spent money to save Wenlong was largely the same as Wenlong's account. The District Chief considered Wang's appearance to be strange and evil, seemingly non-human, and it was difficult to believe whether he had spent 30 yuan to redeem Wenlong. It might be a cover-up. It was also possible that he was familiar with the bandits, so not only was he guilty of hiding a girl under the age of 20, but he was also suspected of being involved in reactionary activities. He ordered that all the people be sent to the Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

Under Family Pressure, a Young Man Attempts to Drown Himself in the Huangpu River

Spitting Blood...Quitting His Job

Mother...No Food to Eat

Extremely Angry...Jumps into the Huangpu River

Fortunately...Rescued

At 9:30 yesterday morning, Yu Rongzhai's son, Deng'ao, 18 years old, a handsome young man residing at No. 99 Nanshi Nanqu Street, boarded the Dongjiadu ferry. When the boat reached the middle of the river, he suddenly took out a card from his pocket, on which was written his address and house number in detail, and placed it on the bow of the boat. He then attempted to jump into the river. Fortunately, a passenger on the boat saw his strange behavior and grabbed him, preventing him from falling into the river. When asked about the reason, he said that he had initially studied at the Black Moon Printing Ink Company, but because he was weak and sickly and the company's duties were extremely tedious, he contracted hemoptysis. He had no choice but to resign and return home to recuperate, but unexpectedly, his mother was unreasonable and often beat and scolded him. He was responsible for all the chores in the house, even washing clothes, cooking, and washing dishes. His mother was often dissatisfied. Because he currently had no job, he had to endure it and remain calm. However, yesterday morning, he was cleaning up in his room when his mother cursed him again and said that he would not be allowed to eat at home from now on. He thought to himself that he had resigned because he was sick, but his mother was forcing him like this, which was really meaningless. He had a small conflict with his mother and angrily left the house. But the world was vast and he had nowhere to go, and he unconsciously had a thought of seeking death, and so on. The boatman, Mr. Li, comforted him with kind words and escorted him back to his home, instructing his mother not to abuse him again in the future.

Reopening of the Far East Bank

The Far East Bank in this city suspended operations during the Sino-Russian War. Recently, because China and Russia have reached a peace agreement, it has revived and established a preparatory office at No. 2 Beijing Road. It is scheduled to move into No. 3 Fuzhou Road next Monday to resume business as usual.

Bureau of Works Had Already Taken Action

Second District Office Reports No Injuries

Dilapidated and leaning civilian houses are everywhere in this city. These old houses not only mar the appearance of the city but also endanger public safety. Fortunately, the Municipal Bureau of Works pays attention to taking action, so the number of house collapses and injuries in the areas south of Shanghai and north of the Zhabei District has been greatly reduced compared to before. The recent collapse of eleven buildings at Nos. 246 to 266 Zhaojia Road in the West Gate area was also due to the early action taken and the erection of bamboo fences, so no one was injured. The original text of the report from the Municipal First District Office to the Public Security Bureau on this matter is as follows: (The beginning is omitted) In accordance with your order and the order of the Bureau of Works, we were instructed to maintain the bamboo fences erected around dangerous houses, and a list of dangerous house addresses was issued to our office. We found that bamboo fences have been erected around all the dangerous houses within our jurisdiction. However, the houses at Nos. 246 to 266 Zhaojia Road suddenly collapsed during the continuous heavy rain last month. Fortunately, bamboo fences had already been erected, so no one was injured. Therefore, we hereby submit a document for your information.

Inside the New New Hotel, Obscene Films Screened and Busted

While the Second Reel Was Playing

Detectives Suddenly Rushed In

Arrested Lin and Wang

Each Released on 500 Yuan Bail

Film is now the most popular entertainment, but films that corrupt social morals are rarely shown in major cinemas. However, recently, general hotels often rent out obscene films that are too terrible to look at for guests' temporary viewing. Screening them late at night in the room may relieve the loneliness of the guest's residence, but it is no different from encouraging prostitution. The Public Works Bureau has decided to strictly prohibit such films and has ordered the Chief Inspector to take charge of the matter. Detective Zhang Shaoqi of the Bureau discovered that a guest in Room 37 of the New New Hotel on Guizhou Road had ordered the hotel to rent out the obscene film. The tea boy demanded a rental fee of 50 yuan to screen six reels, later reduced to 45 yuan. On the night before last, the tea boy led local residents Lin Bingsheng and Wang Changsheng to carry the film equipment, etc., to the room. While the second reel was playing, Chinese and foreign detectives suddenly rushed into the room and took Lin and Wang, along with the items, to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Special District Local Court, and the police station prosecuted them for violating social morals. The defendant hired lawyer Ye Fukan for defense. After questioning by Judge Luo, the defendants were ordered to pay 500 yuan each for bail, and the hearing was adjourned.

In the Hundred Thousand Yuan Robbery Case, Two Robbers Once Kidnapped in Longjing

Two Robbers Approved for Transfer to Hangzhou for Trial

Wang E and Wang Yang, two robbers involved in the massive robbery case at the Zhejiang Provincial Bank, were also involved in a kidnapping case in Zhejiang Province. Huan Guanlin, the detective chief of the Jiaxing County Government, came to Shanghai to request their transfer. The Special District Local Court had instructed that the county government prepare an official document for the transfer, as previously reported. It is now learned that the Jiaxing County Government has not yet sent a formal document to the court, but the Zhejiang Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau has sent a detective chief to Shanghai to handle the case and requested the transfer from the police station. A wealthy household, Li, was suddenly kidnapped by bandits in Longjing, not far from Hangzhou, in April of this year. Subsequently, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau successively arrested more than ten suspects, but the hostage's whereabouts were still unknown. After Wang and Wang were arrested by the police station, they confessed to the Li case. Therefore, the Provincial Public Security Bureau came to request their transfer to investigate the hostage's whereabouts from the two robbers, and to have them identify whether the more than ten suspects arrested were all accomplices, to avoid implicating innocent people. The police station authorities, as the court had already approved Jiaxing's request for transfer for investigation with a two-week limit, and Hangzhou also wanted to transfer them but dared not act without authorization. Therefore, yesterday morning, Wang and Wang were transferred to the Special Court again. After questioning by Judge Zhou, it was clarified that Hangzhou wanted to transfer them for the Longjing kidnapping case. Wang and Wang also confessed to kidnapping in Longjing. Therefore, it was ordered that Wang E and Wang Yang be handed over to the detectives to be taken away, with a one-week limit. They must be returned after the expiration.

Zhang Shengrong, from Luodian Maqiao Township in northwestern Wusong, married Zhou Yu, a local widow (previously reported as Wang), as his wife. Qian Xingsheng was extremely resentful and pretended to be a relative of Zhou Yu's and visited Zhou Yu, and conspired this deadly scheme with her. Zhang Shengrong was stabbed in the throat with a knife, and the wound penetrated from the back of his neck. He was killed instantly. Qian Xingsheng, seeing that his goal had been achieved, abandoned the knife and fled. Zhou Yu was taken into custody by the third branch of the Luodian Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, she was sent to the Baoshan County Government, and County Government Examiner Huang went to inspect and fill out the death certificate, ordering the father of the deceased, Zhang Dongsheng, to prepare a coffin for burial. At the same time, he ordered the arrest of the fleeing murderer, Qian Xingsheng, for strict investigation.

Fire Truck Hits Four Female Students

Fire on Dixwell Road

Worker Injured While Saving Blankets

Yesterday afternoon, a sudden fire broke out at Wu Changxing's fence workshop at the intersection of Dixwell Road and Rue A. Foncier, emitting thick smoke and flames.

Page 16

In an instant, more than ten corrugated iron bungalows were reduced to ashes. Fortunately, the nearby fire brigade arrived and extinguished the fire. When the fire broke out, the Zhabei Second Section Fire Brigade immediately dispatched Pumper No. 10492 to the scene to assist the concession's fire truck in extinguishing the fire. It took more than an hour to extinguish the fire. Then, the driver drove back to Zhabei, but before he had gone a few steps, four female students who were going to school came face to face. They were unable to avoid them and were knocked to the ground, bleeding profusely. It was too horrible to witness. Subsequently, Western Constable No. 12 of the Dixwell Road Police Station came and hired a car to send them to Renji Hospital for treatment. The injured are listed below: Yang Yunyun, 13 years old, right foot fractured; her sister, Suying, 11 years old, head and foot injuries, both Cantonese; Shen Yumei, 8 years old, facial skin injuries; Yang Caifu, 11 years old, injuries to both feet. A worker at the workshop, Zhu Mingfu, from Chongming, was burned on the top of his head when he tried to save cotton blankets during the fire. He was sent to Tongren Hospital by his colleagues for treatment.

Seventy-Three-Year-Old Woman Dies Under Car

Zhou Qiu, an elderly woman from Haimen, was 73 years old. She lived in the countryside of Richangqiao and worked as a farmer. Yesterday morning at around 9:00 a.m., she went out alone and passed through the Huining Road Huining Guild Hall corner in the South City. A public bus with number 6115 of the Shanghai South City, which was planned to drive from Longhua to Laobeimen, knocked her down when it arrived there. Her jaw and legs were severely injured, and she fell to the ground unconscious and died immediately. Du Yijun, the police officer No. 26 from the Huining Road Police Station of the Second District General Office, investigated and detained the driver and took him to the district for questioning. The driver confessed that his name was Chuan Yaoshun, 23 years old, from Yiwu, Zhejiang. He explained the circumstances of the accident at that time. Director Wang, according to the confession, immediately ordered the local security chief to report to the court for an inquest and transferred the plaintiff, the deceased's daughter-in-law Zhou Lu, along with the driver, to the court for investigation.

The Charity Property Reorganization Committee Divides Tasks by Shares

Electing Directors for Each Share

Adopting Various Rules

The Shanghai Charity Property Reorganization Committee held its first standing committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Feng Liutang. The meeting passed the committee's operating and deliberation rules and elected Xu Zhendong as the director of the Investigation Share, Zhang Jie as the director of the Audit Share, and Wang Yiting as the director of the Design Share. The committee's detailed operating rules are recorded below:

Detailed Operating Rules of the Shanghai Charity Property Reorganization Committee

(Article 1) The handling of the committee's affairs shall be governed by these detailed rules, unless otherwise stipulated in the committee's constitution. (Article 2) In addition to the chairman's overall management of affairs, the committee may establish the following shares, with committee members concurrently serving in them. Each share shall mutually elect a director to facilitate contact. (1) Investigation Share: concerning the sources, nature, location, amount, use, and environmental conditions of charitable property; the actual amount of revenue; market value estimates; and other matters to be investigated. (2) Audit Share: concerning the auditing of property documents, books, records, and investigation reports. (3) Design Share: concerning the improvement and improvement plans for property management and usage methods. (Article 3) Documents, copying, dispatching, storage, accounting, cashiers, and other matters not belonging to each share shall be handled by the chairman together with the standing committee members on duty and the office staff. (Article 4) Each share shall prepare a report on the cases undertaken at any time, and the report shall be signed by the director and the person in charge and submitted to the chairman for submission to the standing committee for resolution. (Article 5) In addition to the duties stipulated in Article 3, the committee's office staff shall also be directed by the directors of each share to handle various affairs. (Article 6) The committee may hire people in the city who are familiar with charitable undertakings to assist in its affairs when necessary. (Article 7) All members and staff shall keep confidential matters that have not been announced by the committee. (Article 8) If the committee's office staff is insufficient, it may apply to the Social Affairs Bureau to send staff to serve concurrently. (Article 9) If there are any omissions in these detailed rules, they may be proposed by two or more committee members and submitted to the standing committee for amendment.

Xu Renlin Falsely Accuses His Concubine of Running Away

Sentenced to Four Months in Prison or a Fine of 300 Yuan

Xu Renlin, also known as Xu Chunling, a 55-year-old Ningbo native residing at No. 31 Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street, French Concession, reported to the French Concession Police the day before yesterday that his former concubine, Yang Meizhen, had taken advantage of his absence to steal clothing and accessories worth more than 600 yuan and fled without a trace. He requested that the police investigate. Upon receiving the report, the police chief immediately ordered detective Yang Ziquan to investigate. It was discovered that Yang Meizhen had not run away and was safely at home playing mahjong with friends. Xu and Yang Meizhen were both taken to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, it was determined that Xu should not have made a false accusation and had violated Article 180 of the criminal law. He was ordered to post bail. Yesterday, he was summoned to the French Court for investigation. First, the police chief and others explained the previous situation. Then, according to Yang Meizhen's confession, she had married Xu as his concubine. Because Xu was unemployed, they set up a small lottery association in Baoyu Lane. However, due to a lack of care, they had to pawn items every day to make a living, resulting in a large amount of rent owed. She only had minor arguments with Xu and had not stolen anything. She was falsely accused. Xu Renlin confessed that it was due to a temporary mental breakdown that he made the false report and asked for leniency. The Chinese and Western judges ruled that the defendant Xu Renlin was guilty of violating Article 180 of the criminal law and was sentenced to four months in prison or a fine of 300 yuan as a warning.

Ham and Opium

Why Does Zhang Peizhou Look So Flustered?

Yin Zhennan, a squad member of the Second Detachment of the Shanghai City Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team, was patrolling the Suzhopu New Yongan Steamboat on the Tanghong Alley Bridge on the Suzhou Creek at around 3:00 PM yesterday when he noticed a passenger carrying a ham who looked suspicious. Upon inspection, he found that the bottom of the ham was covered with reed mats. After probing with an iron skewer and smelling it, he detected the smell of opium. After removing the reed mats, only the upper half of the ham remained, and the lower end had been cut off. However, the reed mats were full of opium, totaling fifteen large packages weighing tens of taels. The person was immediately detained and taken back to the detachment along with the evidence. During questioning by the patrol officer, the person confessed that his name was Zhang Peizhou, 21 years old, from Shaoxing, and he was engaged in the business of selling goods from the south. He claimed that the ham was entrusted to him by a friend, Zhang Renxiang, to be taken to his hometown of Shaoxing, and he had no knowledge of the contraband opium hidden inside. He was then transferred to the South City Headquarters and, following instructions, was sent to the Third Section of the City Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Tonight's Bicycle Social Race

Tomorrow Afternoon, the Fifth Race Will Be Held

A scene at Weile Garden, a proper autumn chill in the air for an outdoor competition. Though it seems a little late in the season, there are still a few weeks left to sit comfortably and watch the race without being bothered by the wind and dew. The ladies and gentlemen of Shanghai should take advantage of this opportunity, as the amazing performances at Weile Garden are unprecedented in Shanghai and have already earned a good reputation. At the beginning of the season, only ordinary bicycle and motorcycle-paced races were planned. However, when a team of motorcycle experts arrived in Shanghai, they encountered rain, and the dirt track could not be used as desired. They then considered building another track. Once the wooden track at Weile Garden was completed, they immediately held three trial performances, and the audience was amazed and praised it endlessly. The motorcycle races are now at a minimum speed of fifty miles per hour and can easily be increased to sixty or seventy miles per hour. The tracks are only supported by a few uprights, and the rest are almost level with the ground at a 45 degree angle, as if to break the law of gravity. Is this not a spectacle to behold? Not only is the audience shocked and amazed, but even the racers, known as daredevils, are extremely excited. After the guests left on Thursday night, they were still racing to get better results. Ordinary amateur athletes, having seen what the experts can do, are also practicing diligently in the hopes of showing off their skills. As for the ordinary bicycle racers, their results are also excellent. Whether it is a long or short distance race, the speed is extremely fast. However, only a few people have gained a good reputation so far, with the Annam team being the most prominent. Others still need to learn racing techniques and how to win unexpectedly. The Annam team, under the guidance of the French, has more experience and has benefited greatly. However, there are also Chinese teams that can compete with them and go head-to-head. The consultants only point out what needs to be done. At the meeting held on Thursday night, it was announced that the next social race would be held on Saturday (tonight) starting at 9:00 PM. There will be three motorcycle races, as well as amateur races between the McLins team and the Russian team. A special grand competition will be held at 3:00 PM on Sunday afternoon to satisfy the eyes of the people of Shanghai. Ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life, be sure not to miss it!

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor: Regarding the report in your esteemed newspaper a few days ago about the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Kwang Chi" steamer being detained in Wenzhou, and the cargo supervisor Wang Shou Kang being arrested, the facts are not entirely accurate. We hereby send this letter to correct the record. According to the report from the Cargo Handling Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the entire staff of the "Kwang Chi" steamer cargo department reported that the ship arrived in Wenzhou on the 15th of this month, having departed from Shanghai on the 14th. At 11:30 AM, military police fully armed suddenly arrived on the ship, declaring they were there to arrest Liu Fu Lai, creating a very serious situation. However, Liu Fu Lai had already disembarked at that time. After an unsuccessful search, they tied up cargo supervisor Wang Shou Kang and held him hostage. Subsequently, they accompanied soldiers to Liu Fu Lai's home to search, but found no evidence. They then detained Liu's wife at the Public Security Bureau and Wang at the military headquarters, stating that they would not release him until Liu Fu Lai was apprehended. Following this, eleven cargo handlers from the ship appealed to the Wenzhou branch for assistance. Thanks to the efforts of Committee Members Lin and Yang, and Director He of the China Merchants branch office, they were able to secure Wang's release on bail at the regiment headquarters, but with the condition that if Liu Fu Lai did not appear within a month, Wang would still be summoned for questioning. The reason for Wang's detention and the crime Liu Fu Lai was accused of were not verified, and the authorities did not clearly state the charges at the time, which is baffling and alarming. We are submitting this urgent letter to your newspaper for clarification and assurance. We remain grateful. Respectfully submitted to the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao newspaper, and best wishes for your well-being. Shanghai Branch of the General Association of the Seamen's Industrial Union of China, September 19th.

To the Editor: Regarding the report in your newspaper this morning that the Second Anniversary Garden Party of this association will be attended by 700 people, whereas in truth it will only host a few dozen attendees made up of our own members and specialized committee members, these are not facts. We fear misunderstandings may easily arise. We hope you can immediately issue a correction. Respectfully submitted to the local news editing department of the Shen Bao newspaper, the Diplomatic Discussion Committee of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, September 19th.

Free Talk

To Be Dismissed with a Laugh

— Hai Ke

A: I don't know how Lao Bing spends his money.

B: I don't know either.

A: But he complains about being broke every day. Yesterday he said he was strapped for cash, and today he says he's in dire straits.

B: Is he trying to borrow money from you?

A: No, I'm asking to borrow from him.

A: All women in the world are heartless.

B: Why are you so distraught? Did you suffer a loss at the hands of women?

A: Last month, I got a lover. Since then, I've been scrimping and saving, borrowing money, and using public funds to take her out in cars, eat at restaurants, and see movies, and I've been constantly buying her things. Yesterday, I proposed to her, but she said I was too extravagant and rejected me with a cold heart!

Girl (sobbing): Father, my precious tortoiseshell cat is lost. I've looked everywhere, but I can't find it.

Father: Good child, don't cry. Tomorrow, I'll write some notices and put them up on the street, and I'll also place an ad in the newspaper.

Girl: Father, but it can't read. How will it see the notices and ads and come back?

Housewife: You must wash this fish more thoroughly. Don't be lazy!

Maid: Fish live in the water all the time. They couldn't be any cleaner. There's no need to wash them.

Snippets of News from the North

— Yu Yang Zhou

A certain gentleman, a relief worker from the Ji Sheng Association, has returned from Shaanxi and Henan and described what he saw and heard, enough to satisfy the desire of the people of Jiangsu to know the truth about that area.

The frequent famines and starvation in Shaanxi and Henan are well-known to people in the South. According to this gentleman, although the area is occupied by Feng Yuxiang's troops, who have established officials and governments, it is essentially a lawless world. Feng's army relies on the land to support hundreds of thousands of starving soldiers, and the amount of requisitioning is extreme. To protect themselves, most of the people in the area have joined the Red Spear Society. Their power is so great that it is frightening. No commoner, nor even a formal military unit of less than a battalion, dares to travel openly, or they will have their weapons confiscated by the Red Spears. Even in areas where the army is stationed, the troops remain in the city, with the gates closed, while the area outside the city is entirely under the control of the Red Spear Society. There is a clear dividing line, and neither side crosses it. If there is an alarm outside the city, the troops inside the city will say, "Our troops are stationed inside the city, and the area outside the city is not our responsibility," and ignore it. In reality, if the city gates are opened, even the defensive perimeter of the city cannot be guaranteed. The Red Spear Society is mostly composed of starving people, so they are very careful to protect relief workers. One day, this gentleman encountered a villager on the road who looked emaciated, with a sallow complexion and ragged clothes. He was carrying a basket, and the gentleman did not pay much attention. Suddenly, he felt the man grab his arm. When he looked back, the tattered clothes in the basket had been lifted, revealing a box of ammunition. The gentleman realized that he was being kidnapped. He said to the man, "I am a relief worker here to save the starving people. Instead of being thanked, I am being detained. How can you be so heartless?" The man immediately apologized and released him. Later, he saw a young man in Western clothes being robbed by several people. He inquired and learned that he was a member of Feng's military headquarters and was being held for ransom. The gentleman was very surprised, but the locals thought it was a normal occurrence and nothing to be alarmed about. It was later learned that a large sum of money was used to redeem him. This was truly a strange affair.

The gentleman also said that after several months of war, wounded soldiers were everywhere in the South, but he had never seen any in the North, nor were there any military hospitals. He was surprised by this, and when he asked the locals, he learned that wounded soldiers in the North, regardless of the extent of their injuries, were simply abandoned to their fate. The reason was that there were so many disaster victims in the area that it was easy to recruit soldiers. Moreover, there were no talented people or medical supplies, so there was no need to provide medical care. The gentleman was shocked to hear this. He also heard that Northerners often considered Southerners to be weak and often used them as servants, and they always had the idea that Northerners should rule the South. Therefore, they concealed news of defeats and did not allow people to see wounded soldiers, in order to project an image of strength. The gentleman was speechless.

The Inventor of 606

— Tian De

The discovery of the syphilis spirochete was made in 1905 by Hofmann and Schaudinn. The discovery of 606 was made in 1907 by Ehrlich. These are all masters of German medicine. Thanks to the efforts of the entire country of Germany in in-depth natural science research over the past hundred years, such outstanding philosophers have been cultivated, achieving such groundbreaking and forward-looking feats. I would like to describe the report by Ehrlich, the inventor of 606, on the successful experiment of 606 at the German Medical and Pharmaceutical Congress in Kahnberg, Germany in 1910. Although the event has passed and become history, the joy and excitement of the time still seems to be present today. Writing about it can inspire future generations to be excited.

Ehrlich said: "606 is the latest invention, and it is generally recognized that it can fundamentally cure syphilis. There are several reasons for this. First, 606 can search for and destroy syphilis spirochetes in the blood cells, eliminating them completely. Second, 606 can stimulate the body's own syphilis-fighting antibodies, enabling the body to eliminate syphilis on its own. This is most evident when treating infantile syphilis. For infants with congenital syphilis who cannot be injected, injecting their mother or wet nurse with 606 is sufficient to transmit the immunity generated in the adult's body to the child through breast milk, achieving a cure. In addition, 606 has another, most difficult-to-explain function. As reported by a professor earlier, a syphilis patient suffered from severe syphilitic ulcers on the upper jaw, causing extreme pain to the point that they could not eat solid food. Therefore, at 2:00 PM, they were injected with 606. By 7:00 PM that day (five hours later), the pain had completely disappeared, and they were able to eat sausage and bread without stopping. The person was overjoyed and hugged the doctor, expressing their gratitude and calling 606 a 'miracle drug.' The reason for such rapid effects is most difficult to explain, so it is impossible not to call it a miracle drug. Other examples include the complete disappearance of systemic secondary syphilis rashes three days after injection with 606, and the self-healing of throat pain or tongue itching in syphilis patients a few hours or even an hour after injection with 606. Even more gratifying news is that 606 is not only an effective drug for treating syphilis, but also for treating diseases other than syphilis, such as relapsing fever, malaria, and yaws. "When he finished speaking, the applause was like a thunderclap. Since then, the name of 606 has spread around the world, especially the new 606 (registered name: Neosalvarsan), which was obtained by Ehrlich after painstakingly researching and experimenting for the 914th time from the derivatives of 606. The injection procedure is even simpler, and the effect is even more rapid. This is truly one of the most exciting pages in the history of medical evolution." (End of Essay)

A Record of Being Deceived into Divorce

— Chen Bo Ying

Zhou Dehou, from Songjiang, Suzhou, married Liu Zhiyun, also from the same village. Liu had studied at a primary school and was quite capable of keeping track of household affairs and writing short notes. Initially, the couple got along very well. After a while, Zhou became acquainted with a woman named Li, and their love grew strong, and they discussed marriage. However, Zhou was cunning. He remained intimate with Liu, even more so than before. Liu's relatives told her what they had heard, but Liu dismissed it as nonsense. One day, Zhou said to Liu, "My dear, although the love between us is steadfast, something has changed. There is a woman in the west of the city who is infatuated with me, but I have rejected her. Now she is seriously ill, and if she could get a letter from you, she might recover. Just let her read it once and then burn it. Heaven is above, and it will see everything. Will you agree to this?" Liu asked what she should write in the letter. Zhou said, "You can write that we are considering divorce because we have disagreements." Liu wrote the letter as requested. Zhou left and did not return for three days. Liu became suspicious, and then a lawyer's letter arrived, stating that since the couple had already divorced, they were free to marry whoever they wanted. Liu fainted upon receiving the letter. When she woke up, she cried bitterly, realizing that all the love in the world was false and that men's hearts are easily changed. However, it was too late for regrets. Liu had a son named Zhou Sui. Zhou said to Liu, "This little baby belongs to me to raise. I cannot let anyone else take care of him." Zhou also said that it was inconvenient for him to breastfeed, so he allowed Liu to raise him. After separating from Zhou, Liu's family's financial situation became difficult. She made a living by sewing and washing clothes for others. When her son grew up a little, she sent him to school. The son studied diligently and always ranked first in his class. He went from primary school to middle school, and from middle school to university. After graduating from university, he became a teacher and lived with his mother. At this time, Zhou Dehou and the woman Li had also divorced. Zhou had some thoughts of getting back together with Liu. He summoned his son and told him, "I feel very guilty about what happened years ago. Now I want to reconcile. I hope you can gently persuade your mother not to disappoint me. Since you have already graduated from university, you should study abroad. If you return with a doctorate, you will be more respected by society. If things go well, I can pay for your studies abroad." The son said, "Since I was young, I have only known my mother, not my father. This matter should be decided by my mother. But if you try to lure me with studying abroad, do you think I would be swayed by a doctorate? Stop dreaming." The son returned and told his mother everything. Neither of them wanted to reconcile with Dehou. Zhou could only sigh deeply.

News from the Publishing Industry: The book "Diary of a University Student" by Hu Tiannong has now been published by the Dongbi Bookstore. The book vividly describes the romantic lives of university students, especially the scandalous affairs and romantic stories of the "University Queens." It is a thick volume and costs five jiao. It is available at the Beixin, Kaiming, Datong, Wenming, Guanghua, and Modern bookstores.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (52)

— Ling Hua

On the 30th, Abbot Shiling, who had recently bought a car, invited me to visit Qingyun Rock to see the Snake Temple, about twenty miles south of Penang. The temple is dedicated to the Qingshui Grand Master. When we arrived, there were many Western and Chinese visitors. I asked where the snakes were, and he pointed to the altar and said, "Haven't you seen them?" I looked up and saw five-colored, mottled objects that looked like flower branches. Those near my body were all flower snakes. Some coiled around the flower branches offered to Buddha, intertwined with the flowers. Others coiled around mirrors on the high places, resembling flower borders. The trays and Buddha boxes were filled with snakes, like grapes, with about three to five, or even seven to eight, intertwined in a ball. If you lifted them with your hand, they would raise their heads. When you let go, they would coil back down. The colors were bright and vibrant, mostly green and flowered. There could be seventy to eighty, or even a hundred, snakes in a room, each one to two feet long. Near the altar, they seemed to be addicted to the smell of incense smoke and didn't want to move. It is said that the snakes come and go on their own, without bothering humans. They have never bitten anyone, just like domesticated animals. People also place chicken eggs for them to eat. I found this very strange, thinking that snakes could also cooperate with humans. Is it really like the old saying, "The wolf and the lamb shall feed together?" It is recorded that a Zen master named Song (whose name I have forgotten) lived in the mountains, and a high-ranking official visited him (also forgetting his name). The official asked if the master had any attendants. The master called out, "Da Kong, Xiao Kong!" Two tigers appeared. The guest was terrified, but the master comforted him, and the tigers retreated. It is indeed true that "high virtue tames dragons and tigers." To the east of the temple was a square pond where a large snake, over ten feet long, was kept and fed chickens. Another monk told me that tens of miles away, in Ipoh, there was a cave with a large snake that could be two miles long. I did not believe it. Another monk said that Snake Mountain in the South Sea also had many snakes that did not harm people, just like the snakes in this temple. It is also said that many people who go to Siam (Thailand) see snakes. The king believes in Buddhism, so people do not harm snakes, and snakes do not harm people. Could this really be true? I will visit Siam soon to investigate.

From the Snake Temple, we went to Penang Hill. The hill was named because the British used it to signal to ships. The mountain is very high, and there is a railway to the top, similar to the Peak Tram in Hong Kong, but the engineering is more solid. There is a waterfall flowing from the top. You have to change cars once in the middle to reach the top. It costs one dollar for a round trip. There is a tea shop at the top and books for sale. There are many red leaves, which look like flowers. Looking closely, you can see that they are actually leaves that have changed color. There are only yellow flowers and green leaves, and the red ones are leaves, not flowers. Standing on the high mountain, you can see that Penang Island is only a small spot. Looking out, you can see the mountains emerging from the clouds, and the clouds merging into the sea. The scenery is excellent. The Kek Lok Si Pagoda can also be seen in the distance. There are Western-style houses on the mountain that can be rented to escape the heat. There is a hotel where each night costs nine dollars. Workers work on the railway on both sides, earning eight jiao to one dollar a day. We visited the machine room, where one or two people turn a large flywheel. The railway is a very large project, and it is quite impressive.

Penang has magnificent mountains and rivers, and the climate is pleasant, making it suitable for health. There are many large trees, so it is very cool outside the bustling city.

Thoughts on Children's Dental Problems

— Tian Xu Wo Sheng

The Shanghai Special City Health Bureau began inspecting the teeth of students in various primary schools in January of this year. According to the reports from dentists, as of June 24th, a total of 5,664 students were examined, and the total number of cavities was 30,110. Only 185 teeth were completely healthy. From this, it can be seen that the number of dental problems accounts for as much as 97%! This is terrible! Humans rely on teeth to chew food. If the teeth are not healthy, chewing will be impaired, leading to indigestion and stomach problems. Humans only get one set of permanent teeth. Girls grow teeth at seven months, lose their milk teeth at seven years, grow their permanent teeth at twenty-one, and lose their teeth at forty-nine. Boys grow teeth at eight months, lose their milk teeth at eight years, grow their permanent teeth at twenty-four, and lose their teeth at sixty-four. If they are not protected during childhood, when the old teeth are being replaced, the old ones will already be decayed, easily trapping food and creating lactic acid. The new ones are like tender shoots that are easily eroded by lactic acid, causing damage. Therefore, damaged teeth should be extracted to prevent them from harming other teeth. In daily life, it is especially important to pay attention to cleanliness. After each meal, children should be instructed to brush their teeth once to rinse away food residue and avoid the bad habit of picking their teeth. The habit of picking teeth can loosen the gums and widen the gaps between teeth, making it easier for food to get trapped, allowing lactic acid to penetrate deep into the tooth chamber. All kinds of dental problems arise from this. The ability of lactic acid to erode tooth enamel is easily proven. Try soaking an eggshell in vinegar overnight, and it will soften, and the lime layer will peel off layer by layer, until only the egg membrane remains. This is because teeth are mostly made up of lime. The outer layer of enamel protects the lime, just like the enamel on porcelainware protects the iron underneath. If the enamel is damaged, the iron will rust, the same principle applies. Therefore, when brushing teeth, never use coarse, hard toothpaste, as it will damage the enamel. The 19th chapter, section 1 of the second publication of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Association of Science Professors and Researchers discusses the use of toothpaste to prevent tooth decay and strengthen the gums. If food residue remains in the gaps between teeth, it can turn into lactic acid and corrode the enamel surface. Therefore, it is necessary to brush teeth with toothpaste every morning and after meals. It also says that the raw materials for making toothpaste must be carefully selected. If it contains excessively coarse powder, the enamel will be damaged. Therefore, the finer the toothpaste, the better. It also says that the best raw material for making toothpaste is magnesium carbonate, because this substance has a pure alkaline nature that can eliminate lactic acid and remove plaque without damaging the enamel. However, this material is very expensive, so calcium carbonate and gypsum powder are often mixed in. From this, it can be seen that it is necessary to choose toothpaste carefully, and making toothpaste for human use is a matter of ethics. If the buyer buys inferior toothpaste and uses it every day, they are destroying their own teeth. Ask yourself, how many times in life can teeth be replaced? If people are careless during childhood and let things take their natural course, irregular teeth will arise, slanting outward, growing horizontally, forming a rake shape, or resembling webbed fingers, all due to the failure to correct them. If brushing teeth is done every morning and before going to bed, it can not only keep the mouth clean but also correct the alignment of the teeth, making them neat. Just like planting tree seedlings, you must support them when they are growing to make them stand straight. In this way, there will be no crooked or bent branches. If you wait until they are grown, you cannot straighten them, even with an ax. Therefore, during the time when children are losing their milk teeth, from the age of seven or eight, their parents, elder siblings, teachers, and guardians should teach them to brush their teeth and develop the habit. The toothbrush should have soft bristles, and the handle should be small and smooth to fit their mouth. If you use hard, coarse brushes, the gums will often be scratched and hurt, and the tender skin of the mouth will be easily damaged. Some rough people like to use hard, coarse toothbrushes and take pleasure in making their gums bleed. This is like the habit of liking scabs and should not be taught. Also, the toothpaste used by children should have less mint and more fruit flavor to appeal to their preferences. Experience shows that most children at the age of seven or eight like banana or lemon flavors, while those from nine to twenty-three like spearmint and fennel flavors. However, sugar is very easy to turn into acid. Try holding any candy in your mouth overnight, and you will definitely have a strange acidic taste in your mouth the next morning. Therefore, sucrose or glucose are not suitable as sugar flavors in toothpaste, and lactose is even worse. Only glycerin should be used, and it should be diluted with a large amount of water so that its taste is appropriately sweet and not too strong. In this way, it will be pleasant and not acidic in the mouth. Diabetics are forbidden to eat sugar, but they are allowed to eat glycerin. This is clear proof. Therefore, I have done in-depth research and feel that there is a need to specially formulate a children's toothpaste that meets the needs of children's dental health. Therefore, I have specialized in manufacturing a children's toothbrush. Its special advantages will be explained in the advertisement, so I will not repeat them here. As for washing products, Wudi brand tooth powder and red mouthwash, as well as the recently improved whitening toothpaste that has a spearmint flavor, are already quite suitable. Now, I have also produced a soft toothpaste with a lemon-banana flavor, packaged in a mirror box so that they can look in the mirror and correct their bad habits while brushing their teeth. This will make protecting their teeth a regular habit and prevent them from stopping and starting inconsistently. Then, according to what is recorded in the old books, women lose their teeth at the age of forty-nine, and men lose their teeth at the age of sixty-four. Before this time of teeth loss, just like trees before late autumn, they should be free from decay. Those who have the responsibility of guiding and managing children should realize that children's dental health is related to their lifelong happiness and should have the same thoughts. They should not regard my words as unimportant.

The Gold Market's Decline Has Stabilized

Fluctuations throughout the day reached 9.3 taels - Yesterday, the gold market situation was exceptionally chaotic, rising and falling with extreme volatility. The fluctuations at certain points reached two or three taels, with a total difference of nine taels between the high and low prices. Initially, dealers anticipated a downward trend, but unexpectedly, large players aggressively bought, reversing the market's direction. Eventually, the market trended upward, almost breaking the 40 tael mark. Simultaneously, foreign exchange unexpectedly strengthened, and banks showed strong buying interest, albeit with a widened ask price of half a point, subtly indicating strength rather than weakness. Early trading saw Yi Yu, Cui Tai, and the Dalian Gang actively bidding, while speculators also covered their short positions. Sellers, such as Yi Feng, Yong Yuan Xing, and Yong Zhi Feng, remained unfazed by the slight increase in prices, maintaining their short positions. Later, while buyers were active, hopes for a swift end to the war and a potential rise in silver prices to recover from its depressed state fueled expectations of a gold price decline. As a result, gold prices plummeted rapidly, falling by five to six taels, briefly dipping below 30 taels. However, around noon, the market unexpectedly surged upwards. Various firms resumed buying, causing prices to jump by over seven taels, a phenomenon that was difficult to comprehend. In the afternoon, demand exceeded supply, and prices continued to climb, soaring from around 35 taels to approximately 40 taels. Exchange rates appeared firm. The final price was around 39 taels. - At the opening of trading this morning, prices slightly declined by four fen. The November opening price was 536 taels and 1 qian, a slight decrease of four fen. Meanwhile, silver prices in the UK and the US each increased by one-eighth. With exchange rates unchanged, market sentiment remained weak. Zhi Feng, Yong, and others began selling, causing prices to drop by four taels, reaching 32 taels and 23 qian. Prices then recovered slightly, gaining two taels. Subsequently, upon the announcement of the first market price at 34 taels, followed by a widening ask of 1.25 US dollars, the decline in gold prices was limited to 0.75, reducing the decline to 33 taels and 12 qian. However, prices immediately rebounded, with Sumitomo and Huabi trading January US dollars at 41.25 yuan and Datong and HSBC trading December UK gold at 8.3125. Moreover, firms such as Zhi Feng, Yong Cheng Feng, Yong and Yi Yu continued to buy. Large players absorbed the supply, causing prices to rise again, exceeding 7 taels.
